id="cite_ref-NOAA_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flora_and_fauna_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Flora and fauna of Seychelles">Flora and fauna of Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/220px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg" width="220" height="427" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/330px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg/440px-Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_Paradise-flycatcher.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seychelles Paradise-flycatcher</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/220px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/330px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG/440px-Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3467" data-file-height="3751" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aldabra_Female_on_Curieuse.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Aldabra giant tortoise</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nerita_plicata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nerita_plicata.jpg/220px-Nerita_plicata.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nerita_plicata.jpg/330px-Nerita_plicata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Nerita_plicata.jpg/440px-Nerita_plicata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1219" data-file-height="1219" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nerita_plicata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Nerita plicata</i> on Mahe island</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/220px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/330px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg/440px-Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2179" data-file-height="2792" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bird_flocks_Bird_Island_Seychelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bird flocks Bird Island Seychelles</div></div></div>\n<p>Seychelles is among the world\'s leading countries to protect lands for <a href="/wiki/Threatened_species" title="Threatened species">threatened species</a>, allocating 42% of its territory for <a href="/wiki/Conservation" title="Conservation">conservation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Like many fragile island ecosystems, Seychelles saw the loss of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> when humans first settled in the area, including the disappearance of most of the <a href="/wiki/Giant_tortoise" title="Giant tortoise">giant tortoises</a> from the granitic islands, the felling of coastal and mid-level forests, and the extinction of species such as the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_chestnut-flanked_white-eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychelles chestnut-flanked white-eye">chestnut flanked white eye</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_parakeet" title="Seychelles parakeet">Seychelles parakeet</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile" title="Saltwater crocodile">saltwater crocodile</a>. However, extinctions were far fewer than on islands such as <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, partly due to a shorter period of human occupation (since 1770). Seychelles today is known for success stories in protecting its flora and fauna. The rare <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_black_parrot" title="Seychelles black parrot">Seychelles black parrot</a>, the national bird of the country, is now protected.\n</p><p>The granitic islands of Seychelles are home to about 75 endemic plant species, with a further 25 or so species in the <a href="/wiki/Aldabra" title="Aldabra">Aldabra</a> group. Particularly well-known is the <a href="/wiki/Coco_de_mer" class="mw-redirect" title="Coco de mer">coco de mer</a>, a species of palm that grows only on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a> and neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Curieuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Curieuse">Curieuse</a>. Sometimes nicknamed the "love nut" because the shape of its "double" coconut resembles buttocks, the coco-de-mer produces the world\'s heaviest seed. The <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Jellyfish tree">jellyfish tree</a> is to be found in only a few locations on <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mah\xc3\xa9, Seychelles">Mahe</a>. This strange and ancient plant in a genus of its own (<i><a href="/wiki/Medusagyne" title="Medusagyne">Medusagyne</a></i>) seems to reproduce only in cultivation and not in the wild. Other unique plant species include Wright\'s gardenia (<i><a href="/wiki/Rothmannia_annae" title="Rothmannia annae">Rothmannia annae</a></i>) found only on <a href="/wiki/Aride_Island" title="Aride Island">Aride Island</a> Special Reserve.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Freshwater_crab" title="Freshwater crab">freshwater crab</a> genus <i><a href="/wiki/Seychellum" title="Seychellum">Seychellum</a></i> is endemic to the granitic Seychelles, and a further 26 species of crabs and five species of <a href="/wiki/Hermit_crab" title="Hermit crab">hermit crabs</a> live on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Haig_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haig-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Aldabra_giant_tortoise" title="Aldabra giant tortoise">Aldabra giant tortoise</a> now populates many of the islands of Seychelles; the Aldabra population is the largest remaining. These unique reptiles can be found even in captive herds. The granitic islands of Seychelles may support distinct species of <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_giant_tortoise" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychelles giant tortoise">Seychelles giant tortoises</a>; the status of the different populations is currently unclear.\n</p><p>There are several unique species of orchid on the islands.\n</p><p>Seychelles hosts some of the largest <a href="/wiki/Bird_colony" title="Bird colony">seabird colonies</a> in the world, notably on the outer islands of Aldabra and Cosmoledo. In <a href="/wiki/Granitic_Seychelles" title="Granitic Seychelles">granitic Seychelles</a> the largest colonies are on <a href="/wiki/Aride_Island" title="Aride Island">Aride Island</a> including the world\'s largest numbers of two species. Sooty terns also breed on the islands. Other birds include Cattle egrets (<i>Bubulcus ibis</i>) and Fairy terns (<i>Gygis alba</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The marine life around the islands, especially the more remote coral islands, can be spectacular. More than 1,000 species of fish have been recorded.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">Environmental issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the use of <a href="/wiki/Speargun" title="Speargun">spearguns</a> and dynamite for fishing was banned through efforts of local conservationists in the 1960s, the wildlife is unafraid of <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkelers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">divers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Coral_bleaching" title="Coral bleaching">Coral bleaching</a> in 1998 has damaged most reefs, but some reefs show healthy recovery (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette Island</a>).\n</p><p>Despite huge disparities across nations, Seychelles claims to have achieved nearly all of its <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  17 MDGS and 169 targets have been achieved.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  Environmental protection is becoming a cultural value.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Their government\'s Seychelles Climate Guide describes the nation\'s climate as rainy, with a dry season with an ocean economy in the ocean regions.  The Southeast Trades is on the decline but still fairly strong.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  Reportedly, weather patterns there are becoming less predictable.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Seychelles" title="Demographics of Seychelles">Demographics of Seychelles</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Indo-Seychellois" title="Indo-Seychellois">Indo-Seychellois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sino-Seychellois" title="Sino-Seychellois">Sino-Seychellois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Seychellois Creole People">Seychellois Creole People</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Franco-Seychellois" title="Franco-Seychellois">Franco-Seychellois</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_(Seychelles).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg/220px-Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg/330px-Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg/440px-Victoria_%28Seychelles%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_(Seychelles).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria, Seychelles</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Seychelles_demography.png/220px-Seychelles_demography.png" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Seychelles_demography.png/330px-Seychelles_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Seychelles_demography.png/440px-Seychelles_demography.png 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Demographics of Seychelles, Data of <a href="/wiki/FAO" class="mw-redirect" title="FAO">FAO</a>, year 2005&#160;; Number of inhabitants in thousands.</div></div></div>\n<p>When the British gained control of the islands during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, they allowed the French upper class to retain their land. Both the French and British settlers used enslaved Africans, and although the British prohibited slavery in 1835, African workers continued to come. Thus the <i>Gran blan</i> ("big whites") of French origin dominated economic and political life. The British administration employed Indians on <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servant">indentured servitude</a> to the same degree as in Mauritius resulting in a small Indian population. The Indians, like a similar minority of Chinese, were confined to a merchant class.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Through harmonious socioeconomic policies and developments<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> over the years, today Seychelles is described as a fusion of peoples and cultures. Numerous Seychellois are considered multiracial: blending from African, Asian and European descent to create a modern creole culture. Evidence of this harmonious blend is also revealed in Seychellois food, incorporating various aspects of French, Chinese, Indian and African cuisine.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/220px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg" width="220" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/330px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg/440px-St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1859" data-file-height="2084" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Francis_Church_Mahe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St Francis Church, Mah\xc3\xa9</div></div></div>\n<p>As the islands of the Seychelles had no indigenous population, the current Seychellois are people who have immigrated. The largest ethnic groups were those of African, French, <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> descent. The median age of the Seychellois was 32 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>French and English are official languages along with <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, which is primarily based upon French. However, nowadays the language is often laced with English words and phrases. Including second-language speakers, Seychellois is the most-spoken official language in the Seychelles, followed by French, and lastly by English.<sup id="cite_ref-ethno_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethno-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> 87% of the population speaks Seychellois, 51% speaks French, and 38% speaks English.<sup id="cite_ref-ethno_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethno-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Seychelles" title="Religion in Seychelles">Religion in Seychelles</a></div>\n<p>According to the 2010 census, most Seychellois are Christians: 76.2% were <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Seychelles" title="Catholic Church in Seychelles">Roman Catholic</a>, pastorally served by the exempt <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Port_Victoria_o_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Port Victoria o Seychelles">Diocese of Port Victoria or Seychelles</a> (immediately dependent on the Holy See); 10.6% were Protestant, (<a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> 6.1%, <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostal Assembly</a> 1.5%, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-Day Adventist</a> 1.2%, other Protestant 1.6%).\n</p><p>Hinduism is practiced by 2.4%, and Islam by 1.6%. Other non-Christian faiths accounted for 1.1% of the population while a further 5.9% were non-religious or did not specify a religion.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Seychelles" title="Economy of Seychelles">Economy of Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG/220px-Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG/330px-Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG/440px-Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1179" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahe_Beach_-_author_with_the_sailfish_by_J._Strzelecki.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The sailfish at Mah\xc3\xa9 Beach</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/220px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/330px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg/440px-Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colourful_Skirts_at_Seychelles_Market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Colourful skirts at Seychelles Market</div></div></div>\n<p>During the plantation era, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> were the chief exports. In 1965, during a three-month visit to the islands, futurist <a href="/wiki/Donald_Prell" title="Donald Prell">Donald Prell</a> prepared for the then-<a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> Governor General an economic report containing a scenario for the future of the economy.  Quoting from his report, in the 1960s, about 33% of the working population worked at plantations, and 20% worked in the public or government sector.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Indian Ocean Tracking Station on Mah\xc3\xa9 used by the <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Satellite_Control_Network" title="Air Force Satellite Control Network">Air Force Satellite Control Network</a> was closed in August 1996 after the Seychelles government attempted to raise the rent to more than $10,000,000 per year.\n</p><p>Since independence in 1976, per capita output has expanded to roughly seven times the old near-subsistence level. Growth has been led by the tourist sector, which employs about 30% of the labour force, compared to agriculture which today employs about 3% of the labour force. Despite the growth of tourism, farming and fishing continue to employ some people, as do industries that process coconuts and vanilla.\n</p><p>As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the main export products are processed fish (60%) and non-fillet frozen fish (22%).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The prime agricultural products currently produced in Seychelles include <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>, vanilla, coconuts and cinnamon. These products provide much of the economic support of the locals. Frozen and canned fish, copra, cinnamon and vanilla are the main export commodities.\n</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">worldwide economic crises of 2008</a>, the Seychelles government has prioritised a curbing of the <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a>, including the containment of <a href="/wiki/Social_welfare" class="mw-redirect" title="Social welfare">social welfare</a> costs and further <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> of public enterprises. The government has a pervasive presence in economic activity, with public enterprises active in petroleum product distribution, banking, imports of basic products, telecommunications and a wide range of other businesses. According to the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, which measures the degree of limited government, market openness, regulatory efficiency, rule of law, and other factors, economic freedom has been increasing each year since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The national currency of Seychelles is the <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_rupee" title="Seychellois rupee">Seychellois rupee</a>. Initially tied to a basket of international currencies, it was depegged and allowed to be devalued and float freely in 2008 on the presumed hopes of attracting further foreign investment in the Seychelles economy.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Seychelles" title="Tourism in Seychelles">Tourism in Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_083.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/220px-Seychelles_083.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/330px-Seychelles_083.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Seychelles_083.JPG/440px-Seychelles_083.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_083.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aircraft at <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_International_Airport" title="Seychelles International Airport">Seychelles International Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_hotel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/220px-General_hotel.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/330px-General_hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/General_hotel.jpg/440px-General_hotel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_hotel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Beach resort at Seychelles</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1971, with the opening of <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_International_Airport" title="Seychelles International Airport">Seychelles International Airport</a>, tourism became a significant industry, essentially dividing the economy into plantations and tourism. The tourism sector paid better, and the plantation economy could only expand so far. The plantation sector of the economy declined in prominence, and tourism became the primary industry of Seychelles.\n</p><p>In recent years the government has encouraged foreign investment to upgrade hotels and other services. These incentives have given rise to an enormous amount of investment in real estate projects and new resort properties, such as project TIME, distributed by the World Bank, along with its predecessor project MAGIC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Despite its growth, the vulnerability of the tourist sector was illustrated by the sharp drop in 1991\xe2\x80\x931992 due largely to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since then the government has moved to reduce the dependence on tourism by promoting the development of farming, fishing, small-scale manufacturing and most recently the offshore financial sector, through the establishment of the Financial Services Authority and the enactment of several pieces of legislation (such as the International Corporate Service Providers Act, the International Business Companies Act, the Securities Act, the Mutual Funds and Hedge Fund Act, amongst others).\n</p><p>During March 2015, Seychelles allocated <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Island" title="Assumption Island">Assumption Island</a> to be developed by India.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Although multinational oil companies have explored the waters around the islands, no oil or gas has been found. In 2005, a deal was signed with US firm Petroquest, giving it exploration rights to about 30,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> around Constant, Topaz, Farquhar and Co\xc3\xabtivy islands until 2014. Seychelles imports oil from the Persian Gulf in the form of refined petroleum derivatives at the rate of about 5,700 barrels per day (910&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d).\n</p><p>In recent years oil has been imported from Kuwait and also from Bahrain. Seychelles imports three times more oil than is needed for internal uses because it re-exports the surplus oil in the form of <a href="/wiki/Bunker_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bunker fuel">bunker</a> for ships and aircraft calling at <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mah\xc3\xa9, Seychelles">Mah\xc3\xa9</a>. There are no refining capacities on the islands. Oil and gas imports, distribution and re-export are the responsibility of Seychelles Petroleum (Sepec), while oil exploration is the responsibility of the Seychelles National Oil Company (SNOC).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Seychelles" title="Women in Seychelles">Women in Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/200px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/300px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg/400px-Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="2288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clock_Tower_-Victoria_-Seychelles2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The district clock tower in the centre of the capital <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Seychelles" title="Victoria, Seychelles">Victoria</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Seychellois society is essentially <a href="/wiki/Matriarchy" title="Matriarchy">matriarchal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hr_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Mothers tend to be dominant in the household, controlling most expenditures and looking after the interests of the children.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unwed_mother" class="mw-redirect" title="Unwed mother">Unwed mothers</a> are the societal norm, and the law requires fathers to <a href="/wiki/Child_support" title="Child support">support their children</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hr_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hr-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Men are important for their earning ability, but their domestic role is relatively peripheral.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Seychelles" title="Education in Seychelles">Education in Seychelles</a></div>\n<p>Until the mid 19th century, little formal education was available in Seychelles. The Catholic and Anglican churches opened mission schools in 1851. The Catholic mission later operated boys\' and girls\' secondary schools with religious brothers and nuns from abroad even after the government became responsible for them in 1944.\n</p><p>A teacher training college opened in 1959, when the supply of locally trained teachers began to grow, and in short time many new schools were established. Since 1981 a system of free education has been in effect, requiring attendance by all children in grades one to nine, beginning at age five. Ninety percent of all children attend nursery school at age four.\n</p><p>The literacy rate for school-age children rose to more than 90% by the late 1980s. Many older Seychellois had not been taught to read or write in their childhood; adult education classes helped raise adult literacy from 60% to a claimed 100% in 2014.\n</p><p>There are a total of 68 schools in Seychelles. The public school system consists of 23 <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">cr\xc3\xa8ches</a>, 25 primary schools and 13 secondary schools. They are located on <a href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_Seychelles" title="Mah\xc3\xa9, Seychelles">Mah\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Digue" title="La Digue">La Digue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silhouette_Island" title="Silhouette Island">Silhouette</a>. Additionally, there are three private schools: \xc3\x89cole Fran\xc3\xa7aise, International School and the Independent School. All the private schools are on Mah\xc3\xa9, and the International School has a branch on <a href="/wiki/Praslin" title="Praslin">Praslin</a>. There are seven post-secondary (non-tertiary) schools: the Seychelles Polytechnic, School of Advanced Level Studies, Seychelles Tourism Academy, University of Seychelles Education, Seychelles <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Technology">Institute of Technology</a>, Maritime Training Center, Seychelles Agricultural and Horticultural Training Center and the National Institute for Health and Social Studies.\n</p><p>The administration launched plans to open a university in an attempt to slow down the <a href="/wiki/Brain_drain" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain drain">brain drain</a> that has occurred. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Seychelles" title="University of Seychelles">University of Seychelles</a>, initiated in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a>, opened on 17 September 2009 in three locations, and offers qualifications from the University of London.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Seychelles">Cuisine of Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/220px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" width="220" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/330px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg/440px-Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="1703" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cutting_coconuts_Seychelles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cutting open young coconuts for drinking, Seychelles</div></div></div>\n<p>Staple foods include fish, seafood and <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> dishes, often accompanied with rice.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Fish dishes are cooked in several ways, such as steamed, <a href="/wiki/Grilling" title="Grilling">grilled</a>, wrapped in <a href="/wiki/Banana_leaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Banana leaves">banana leaves</a>, baked, salted and <a href="/wiki/Smoking_(cooking)" title="Smoking (cooking)">smoked</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Curry dishes with rice are also a significant aspect of the country\'s cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PT_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Additional food staples include coconut, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">mangoes</a> and <i>kordonnyen fish</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Dishes are often garnished with fresh flowers.<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Chicken dishes, such as chicken curry and <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Coconut curry<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dal" title="Dal">Dhal</a> (lentils)<sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Fish curry<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Saffron_rice" title="Saffron rice">Saffron rice</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tingay_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tingay-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Fresh <a href="/wiki/Tropical_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical fruit">tropical fruits</a><sup id="cite_ref-Lonely_Planet_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lonely_Planet-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GOT_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOT-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ladob" title="Ladob">Ladob</a> is eaten either as a savoury dish or as a dessert. The dessert version usually consists of ripe <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a> (but may also include <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a> or even <a href="/wiki/Soursop" title="Soursop">corossol</a>) boiled with coconut milk, sugar, <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a> and vanilla in the form of a pod until the fruit is soft and the sauce is creamy.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpin_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpin-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The savoury dish usually includes salted fish, cooked in a similar fashion to the dessert version, with plantain, cassava and breadfruit, but with salt used in place of sugar (and omitting vanilla).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shark_chutney" title="Shark chutney">Shark chutney</a> typically consists of boiled skinned shark, finely mashed, and cooked with squeezed <a href="/wiki/Bilimbi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilimbi">bilimbi</a> juice and <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">lime</a>. It is mixed with onion and spices, and the onion is fried and it is cooked in oil.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpin_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpin-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Vegetables<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_44-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GOT_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GOT-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Seychelles" title="Music of Seychelles">Music of Seychelles</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Seychelles" title="Music of Seychelles">music of Seychelles</a> is diverse, a reflection of the fusion of cultures through its history. The <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> of the islands incorporates multiple influences in a syncretic fashion, including African rhythms, aesthetic and instrumentation\xe2\x80\x94such as the zez and the bom (known in Brazil as <a href="/wiki/Berimbau" title="Berimbau">berimbau</a>), European <a href="/wiki/Contredanse_(organisation)" title="Contredanse (organisation)">contredanse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">polka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazurka" title="Mazurka">mazurka</a>, French folk and pop, <a href="/wiki/Sega_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Sega music">sega</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and R\xc3\xa9union, <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">taarab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a> and other pan-African genres, and <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcadia" title="Arcadia">Arcadian</a> music.\n</p><p>A form of percussion music called contombley is popular, as is <a href="/wiki/Moutya" class="mw-redirect" title="Moutya">Moutya</a>, a fusion of native folk rhythms with Kenyan <a href="/wiki/Benga_music" title="Benga music">benga</a>. Kontredans (based on European contredanse) is popular, especially in District and School competitions during the annual Festival Kreol (International Creole Festival). Moutya playing and dancing can often be seen at beach bazaars. Their main languages are <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a> of the French language, French and English.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_telecommunications">Media and telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Media and telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_and_telecommunications_in_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Media and telecommunications in Seychelles">Media and telecommunications in Seychelles</a></div>\n<p>The main daily newspaper is the <i><a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Nation" title="Seychelles Nation">Seychelles Nation</a></i>, dedicated to local government views and current affairs and topics. Other political parties operate other papers such as <i>Regar</i>. Foreign newspapers and magazines are readily available in most bookshops and newsagents. The papers are mostly written in <a href="/wiki/Seychellois_Creole" title="Seychellois Creole">Seychellois Creole</a>, French and English.\n</p><p>The main television and radio network is operated by the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Seychelles Broadcasting Corporation">Seychelles Broadcasting Corporation</a> which offers locally produced news and discussion programmes in the Seychellois Creole language. Broadcasts run between 3pm and 11:30pm on weekdays and longer hours during the weekends. There are also imported English and French language television programmes imported on Seychellois terrestrial television and international satellite television has grown rapidly in recent years.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The most popular sport in Seychelles is basketball, which has particularly developed in this decade.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The country\'s <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_national_basketball_team" title="Seychelles national basketball team">national team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2015_African_Games" title="Basketball at the 2015 African Games">2015 African Games</a>, its greatest accomplishment to date. There, the team competed against some of the continent\'s largest countries such as <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_basketball_team" title="Egypt national basketball team">Egypt</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Seychelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Seychelles">Military of Seychelles</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria,_Seychelles.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/220px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/330px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG/440px-INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria%2C_Seychelles.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="625" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:INS_Teg_approaching_Port_Victoria,_Seychelles.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/INS_Teg" title="INS Teg">INS&#160;<i>Teg</i></a> approaching Port Victoria, Seychelles</div></div></div>\n<p>The Military of Seychelles is the Seychelles People\'s Defence Force which consists of a number of distinct branches: an Infantry Unit and Coast Guard, Air Force and a Presidential Protection Unit. India has played and continues to play a key role developing the military of Seychelles. After handing over two <a href="/wiki/Trinkat-class_patrol_vessel" title="Trinkat-class patrol vessel">SDB Mk5 patrol vessels</a> namely INS Tarasa and INS Tarmugli to <a href="/wiki/Seychelles_Coast_Guard" title="Seychelles Coast Guard">Seychelles Coast Guard</a>, built by <a href="/wiki/GRSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GRSE">GRSE</a> which were subsequently renamed SCG Constant and SCG Topaz, India also gifted a <a href="/wiki/Dornier_Flugzeugwerke" title="Dornier Flugzeugwerke">Dornier</a> Maritime Patrol aircraft built by <a href="/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics_Limited" title="Hindustan Aeronautics Limited">Hindustan Aeronautics Limited</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> India also signed a pact to develop <a href="/wiki/Assumption_Island" title="Assumption Island">Assumption Island</a>, one of the 115 islands that make up the country. Spread over 11&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4&#160;sq&#160;mi), it is strategically located in the Indian Ocean, north of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. The island is being leased for the development of infrastructure, a euphemism for developing strategic assets by India.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incarceration">Incarceration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Incarceration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_incarceration_rate" title="List of countries by incarceration rate">List of countries by incarceration rate</a></div>\n<p>In 2014, Seychelles had the highest incarceration rate in the world of 799 prisoners per 100,000 population, exceeding the United States rate by 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> However, the country\'s actual population is less than 100,000; as of September 2014, Seychelles had 735 actual prisoners, 6% of whom were female, incarcerated in three prisons.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_piracy">Modern piracy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Modern piracy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Seychelles is a key participant in the fight against Indian Ocean <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">piracy</a> mainly by Somalis.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Former president <a href="/wiki/James_Michel" title="James Michel">James Michel</a> said that piracy costs between $7 million \xe2\x80\x93 $12 million a year to the international community: "The pirates cost 4% of the Seychelles <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, including direct and indirect costs for the loss of boats, fishing, and tourism, and the indirect investment for the maritime security," factors affecting local fishing \xe2\x80\x93 one of the country\'s main national resources \xe2\x80\x93 which had a 46% loss in 2008\xe2\x80\x9309.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> International contributions of patrol boats, planes or drones have been provided to help Seychelles combat sea piracy.<sup id="cite_ref-wc_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wc-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seychelles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
